```sql
    AND ra.year BETWEEN 2007 AND 2009
```

--- [224] db=formula_1 difficulty=challenging ---
Q: What is the average time in seconds of champion for each year, before year 1975?
EVIDENCE: only champion's finished time is represented by 'HH:MM:SS.mmm'; finished the game refers to time is not null; before year 1975 refers to year < 1975;
GOLD: WITH time_in_seconds AS ( SELECT T2.year, T2.raceId, T1.positionOrder, CASE WHEN T1.positionOrder = 1 THEN (CAST(SUBSTR(T1.time, 1, 1) AS REAL) * 3600) + (CAST(SUBSTR(T1.time, 3, 2) AS REAL) * 60) + CAST(SUBSTR(T1.time, 6,2) AS REAL )   + CAST(SUBSTR(T1.time, 9) AS REAL)/1000 ELSE 0 END AS time_seconds FROM results AS T1 INNER JOIN races AS T2 ON T1.raceId = T2.raceId WHERE T1.time IS NOT NULL ), champion_time AS ( SELECT year, raceId, time_seconds FROM time_in_seconds WHERE positionOrder = 1 ) SELECT year, AVG(time_seconds) FROM champion_time WHERE year < 1975 GROUP BY year HAVING AVG(time_seconds) IS NOT NULL
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this question step by step:

1. **What we need**: Average time in seconds of champions for each year, before year 1975
2. **Key conditions**:
   - Only champion's finished time is represented by 'HH:MM:SS.mmm' format
   - Finished the game means time is not null
   - Before year 1975 means year < 1975
3. **Champions**: Based on the schema, champions would be drivers who finished in position 1 (first place)
4. **Time conversion**: We need to convert 'HH:MM:SS.mmm' format to seconds

Let me trace through the schema:
- The `results` table contains race results with `time` field and `position` field
- We need to filter for position = 1 (champions) and time is not null
- We need to filter for year < 1975
- We need to convert time format to seconds and calculate average

Looking at the schema more carefully:
- `results` table has `time` field (text) and `position` field
- `races` table has `year` field and `raceId` 
- We need to join these tables to get the year information

The time format in the examples is like '1:34:50.616' which is HH:MM:SS.mmm

To convert this to seconds:
- Split by ':' to get hours, minutes, seconds
- Hours * 3600 + Minutes * 60 + Seconds

Let me write the query:

```sql
SELECT 
    r.year,
    AVG(
        CAST(SUBSTR(res.time, 1, INSTR(res.time, ':') - 1) AS INTEGER) * 3600 +
        CAST(SUBSTR(res.time, INSTR(res.time, ':') + 1, INSTR(res.time, ':', INSTR(res.time, ':') + 1) - INSTR(res.time, ':') - 1) AS INTEGER) * 60 +
        CAST(SUBSTR(res.time, INSTR(res.time, ':', INSTR(res.time, ':') + 1) + 1, INSTR(res.time, '.') - INSTR(res.time, ':', INSTR(res.time, ':') + 1) - 1) AS REAL)
    ) AS average_time_seconds
FROM results res
JOIN races r ON res.raceId = r.raceId
WHERE res.position = 1 
    AND res.time IS NOT NULL 
    AND r.year < 1975
    AND res.time LIKE '%:%:%'
GROUP BY r.year
ORDER BY r.year;
```

--- [225] db=formula_1 difficulty=simple ---
Q: What is the fastest lap number of the champion in 2009?
EVIDENCE: in 2009 refers to year = 2009; Only the time of the champion shows in the format of "hour: minutes: seconds.millionsecond"
GOLD: SELECT T1.fastestLap FROM results AS T1 INNER JOIN races AS T2 on T1.raceId = T2.raceId WHERE T2.year = 2009 AND T1.time LIKE '_:%:__.___'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me think through this step by step.

1. I need to find the champion in 2009
2. The champion is the driver with the highest points in the 2009 season
3. I need to find the fastest lap number for this champion in 2009

Let me trace through the schema:
- The `driverStandings` table contains driver standings with points for each race
- The `races` table has the year information
- The `results` table has the fastestLap information
- I need to join these tables to find the champion and their fastest lap

Steps:
1. First, I need to identify the champion in 2009 (driver with highest total points)
2. Then, I need to find the fastest lap number for that driver in 2009

Looking more carefully at the question: "What is the fastest lap number of the champion in 2009?"

The question asks for the fastest lap number (not time), and it mentions "Only the time of the champion shows in the format of 'hour: minutes: seconds.millionsecond'" - this seems to be additional context about the data format, but the actual question is about the fastest lap number.

Let me reconsider: The fastest lap number would be the lap number where the driver achieved their fastest lap time. Looking at the schema:
- `results` table has `fastestLap` column which seems to be the lap number where the fastest lap was achieved
- `results` table also has `fastestLapTime` which is in the format mentioned

So I need to:
1. Find the champion driver in 2009 (highest total points)
2. Get their fastest lap number from the results table

```sql
SELECT r.fastestLap
FROM results r
JOIN races ra ON r.raceId = ra.raceId
WHERE ra.year = 2009
AND r.driverId = (
    SELECT driverId
    FROM driverStandings ds
    JOIN races r2 ON ds.raceId = r2.raceId
    WHERE r2.year = 2009
    GROUP BY driverId
    ORDER BY SUM(points) DESC
    LIMIT 1
)
AND r.fastestLap IS NOT NULL
ORDER BY r.fastestLap
LIMIT 1
```

--- [227] db=formula_1 difficulty=challenging ---
Q: From 2000 to 2005, what percentage of drivers who were born before 1985 and the lap numbers were over 50?
EVIDENCE: born before 1985 refers to year(dob)<1985; in 2000 to 2005 refers to year between 2000 and 2005; percentage = Divide(COUNT(driverId where year (dob) <1985 and laps >50),COUNT(DriverID where year between 2000 and 2005) *100;
GOLD: SELECT CAST(SUM(IIF(STRFTIME('%Y', T3.dob) < '1985' AND T1.laps > 50, 1, 0)) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(*) FROM results AS T1 INNER JOIN races AS T2 on T1.raceId = T2.raceId INNER JOIN drivers AS T3 on T1.driverId = T3.driverId WHERE T2.year BETWEEN 2000 AND 2005
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the question**: 
   - We need to find the percentage of drivers born before 1985 who had laps > 50
   - But only for races between 2000 and 2005
   - The percentage formula is: (Count of drivers born before 1985 with laps > 50) / (Count of all drivers in races 2000-2005) * 100

2. **Key tables needed**:
   - `drivers` - for dob (date of birth)
   - `results` - for laps and raceId
   - `races` - for year filtering

3. **Steps to build the query**:
   - First, I need to identify drivers born before 1985 who had laps > 50 in races between 2000-2005
   - Then, I need to count all drivers who participated in races between 2000-2005
   - Finally, calculate the percentage

4. **Important considerations**:
   - Need to join drivers, results, and races tables
   - Filter races by year between 2000 and 2005
   - For the numerator, filter drivers born before 1985 AND laps > 50
   - For the denominator, count all distinct drivers in races 2000-2005

Let me construct the query:

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN d.dob < '1985-01-01' AND r.laps > 50 THEN 1 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / 
    COUNT(DISTINCT d.driverId) AS percentage
FROM drivers d
JOIN results r ON d.driverId = r.driverId
JOIN races ra ON r.raceId = ra.raceId
WHERE ra.year BETWEEN 2000 AND 2005
```

--- [228] db=formula_1 difficulty=moderate ---
Q: How many French drivers who obtain the laptime less than 02:00.00?
EVIDENCE: lap time less than 02:00.00 refers to seconds < 120;
GOLD: SELECT COUNT(T1.driverId) FROM drivers AS T1 INNER JOIN lapTimes AS T2 on T1.driverId = T2.driverId WHERE T1.nationality = 'French' AND (CAST(SUBSTR(T2.time, 1, 2) AS INTEGER) * 60 + CAST(SUBSTR(T2.time, 4, 2) AS INTEGER) + CAST(SUBSTR(T2.time, 7, 2) AS REAL) / 1000) < 120
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the number of French drivers who obtained a lap time less than 02:00.00.

Let me break down the requirements:
1. French drivers (from drivers table where nationality = 'French')
2. Lap time less than 02:00.00 (which means seconds < 120)
3. Count how many such drivers there are

Looking at the schema:
- The `drivers` table has `driverId` and `nationality`
- The `lapTimes` table has `driverId` and `time` (stored as text in format like '1:49.088')
- I need to join these tables and filter for French drivers with lap times < 120 seconds

First, I need to understand how to convert the time format. The time is stored as text in format like '1:49.088' which means 1 minute 49.088 seconds = 1*60 + 49.088 = 109.088 seconds.

To find lap times < 02:00.00 (120 seconds), I need to:
1. Join drivers and lapTimes tables on driverId
2. Filter for French nationality
3. Convert the time string to seconds and filter for < 120
4. Count distinct drivers (since one driver might have multiple laps)

Let me write the query:

```sql
SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT d.driverId)
FROM drivers d
JOIN lapTimes lt ON d.driverId = lt.driverId
WHERE d.nationality = 'French'
  AND CAST(SUBSTR(lt.time, 1, INSTR(lt.time, ':') - 1) AS INTEGER) * 60 + 
      CAST(SUBSTR(lt.time, INSTR(lt.time, ':') + 1) AS REAL) < 120
```

Q: On what year did the youngest driver had his first qualifying race? Also state the name, date and time of the race.

GOLD: SELECT T3.year, T3.name, T3.date, T3.time FROM qualifying AS T1 INNER JOIN drivers AS T2 on T1.driverId = T2.driverId INNER JOIN races AS T3 on T1.raceId = T3.raceId WHERE T1.driverId = ( SELECT driverId FROM drivers ORDER BY dob DESC LIMIT 1 ) ORDER BY T3.date ASC LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the year when the youngest driver had his first qualifying race, along with the race details.

Let me break this down step by step:

1. First, I need to identify the youngest driver (the one with the most recent birth date - largest dob value)
2. Then, I need to find when this driver first qualified (earliest qualifying record)
3. Get the race details (year, date, time) for that first qualifying race

Let me trace through the relationships:
- Drivers table has dob (date of birth)
- Qualifying table links drivers to races
- Races table has year, date, and time

Steps:
1. Find the youngest driver (MAX(dob))
2. Find all qualifying records for this driver
3. Find the earliest race (MIN(races.date)) among these qualifying records
4. Get the race details (year, date, time)

```sql
SELECT 
    r.year,
    r.date,
    r.time
FROM drivers d
JOIN qualifying q ON d.driverId = q.driverId
JOIN races r ON q.raceId = r.raceId
WHERE d.driverId = (
    SELECT driverId 
    FROM drivers 
    WHERE dob = (
        SELECT MAX(dob) 
        FROM drivers
    )
)
AND r.date = (
    SELECT MIN(r2.date)
    FROM drivers d2
    JOIN qualifying q2 ON d2.driverId = q2.driverId
    JOIN races r2 ON q2.raceId = r2.raceId
    WHERE d2.driverId = (
        SELECT driverId 
        FROM drivers 
        WHERE dob = (
            SELECT MAX(dob) 
            FROM drivers
        )
    )
)
```

GOLD: SELECT T2.forename, T2.surname FROM pitStops AS T1 INNER JOIN drivers AS T2 on T1.driverId = T2.driverId WHERE T2.nationality = 'German' AND STRFTIME('%Y', T2.dob) BETWEEN '1980' AND '1985' GROUP BY T2.forename, T2.surname ORDER BY AVG(T1.duration) LIMIT 3
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the top 3 German drivers with the shortest average pit stop duration who were born between 1980-1985.

Let me break down the requirements:
1. German drivers (nationality = 'German')
2. Born between 1980-1985 (1980 <= year(dob) <= 1985)
3. Calculate average pit stop duration for each driver

```sql

FROM drivers d
JOIN pitStops ps ON d.driverId = ps.driverId
WHERE d.nationality = 'German' 
  AND strftime('%Y', d.dob) BETWEEN '1980' AND '1985'
GROUP BY d.driverId, d.forename, d.surname
ORDER BY AVG(CAST(ps.duration AS REAL)) ASC
LIMIT 3;
```

1. Join `superhero` with `hero_power` on superhero.id = hero_power.hero_id
2. Join `hero_power` with `superpower` on hero_power.power_id = superpower.id
3. Filter for superhero_name = '3-D Man'
4. Select only the power_name column

```sql

FROM superhero s
```

Q: Which constructor scored most points from Monaco Grand Prix between 1980 and 2010? List the score, name and nationality of this team.
EVIDENCE: Monaco Grand Priz refers to the race; race in year between 1980 and 2010
GOLD: SELECT SUM(T1.points), T2.name, T2.nationality FROM constructorResults AS T1 INNER JOIN constructors AS T2 ON T1.constructorId = T2.constructorId INNER JOIN races AS T3 ON T3.raceid = T1.raceid WHERE T3.name = 'Monaco Grand Prix' AND T3.year BETWEEN 1980 AND 2010 GROUP BY T2.name ORDER BY SUM(T1.points) DESC LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the constructor that scored the most points from Monaco Grand Prix between 1980 and 2010.

Let me think through this step by step:

1. First, I need to identify the Monaco Grand Prix races between 1980 and 2010
2. Then, I need to get the constructor results for those races
3. Sum up the points for each constructor
4. Find the constructor with the maximum points
5. Return the score, name, and nationality of that constructor

Let me trace through the schema:
- Races table has race information including name and year
- ConstructorResults table has points for each constructor in each race
- Constructors table has the constructor name and nationality

Steps:
1. Find races where name = 'Monaco Grand Prix' and year between 1980 and 2010
2. Join with constructorResults to get points for each constructor in those races
3. Join with constructors to get constructor name and nationality
4. Group by constructor to sum up points
5. Order by total points descending and limit to 1 to get the highest

```sql

    c.name,
    c.nationality

WHERE r.name = 'Monaco Grand Prix' 
    AND r.year BETWEEN 1980 AND 2010
GROUP BY c.constructorId, c.name, c.nationality
ORDER BY SUM(cr.points) DESC
LIMIT 1;
```

Q: What is full name of the racer who ranked 1st in the 3rd qualifying race held in the Marina Bay Street Circuit in 2008?

GOLD: SELECT T2.forename, T2.surname FROM qualifying AS T1 INNER JOIN drivers AS T2 on T1.driverId = T2.driverId INNER JOIN races AS T3 ON T1.raceid = T3.raceid WHERE q3 IS NOT NULL AND T3.year = 2008 AND T3.circuitId IN ( SELECT circuitId FROM circuits WHERE name = 'Marina Bay Street Circuit' ) ORDER BY CAST(SUBSTR(q3, 1, INSTR(q3, ':') - 1) AS INTEGER) * 60 + CAST(SUBSTR(q3, INSTR(q3, ':') + 1, INSTR(q3, '.') - INSTR(q3, ':') - 1) AS REAL) + CAST(SUBSTR(q3, INSTR(q3, '.') + 1) AS REAL) / 1000 ASC LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the full name of the racer who ranked 1st in the 3rd qualifying race (q3) held at Marina Bay Street Circuit in 2008.

3. Get the full name (forename and surname) of that driver

Let me trace through the schema:
- Races table has year and circuitId
- Circuits table has circuit names and circuitId
- Qualifying table has q3 times and driverId, and position
- Drivers table has forename and surname

2. Join with qualifying table to find the q3 results
3. Filter for position = 1 in q3

```sql

FROM races r
JOIN circuits c ON r.circuitId = c.circuitId
JOIN qualifying q ON r.raceId = q.raceId

```

Q: As of the present, what is the full name of the youngest racer? Indicate her nationality and the name of the race to which he/she first joined.
EVIDENCE: full name refers to forename+surname; Youngest racer = MAX(dob)
GOLD: SELECT T1.forename, T1.surname, T1.nationality, T3.name FROM drivers AS T1 INNER JOIN driverStandings AS T2 on T1.driverId = T2.driverId INNER JOIN races AS T3 on T2.raceId = T3.raceId ORDER BY JULIANDAY(T1.dob) DESC LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the youngest racer, which means finding the driver with the most recent (maximum) date of birth (dob). Then I need to get their full name (forename + surname), nationality, and the name of the first race they joined.

Let me think through this step by step:

1. First, I need to identify the youngest driver by finding the maximum dob (most recent date of birth)
2. Get their full name (forename + surname) and nationality
3. Find the first race they participated in - this would be the race with the earliest date for that driver
4. Get the name of that race

To find the first race, I need to:
- Join drivers with results to get their race participations
- Join with races to get race names and dates
- Order by race date and take the earliest one

Let me construct the query:

```sql
SELECT 
    d.forename || ' ' || d.surname AS full_name,
    d.nationality,
    r.name AS race_name
FROM drivers d
JOIN results res ON d.driverId = res.driverId
JOIN races r ON res.raceId = r.raceId
WHERE d.dob = (SELECT MAX(dob) FROM drivers)
AND r.date = (
    SELECT MIN(r2.date)
    FROM drivers d2
    JOIN results res2 ON d2.driverId = res2.driverId
    JOIN races r2 ON res2.raceId = r2.raceId
    WHERE d2.driverId = d.driverId
)
LIMIT 1;
```

--- [243] db=formula_1 difficulty=moderate ---
Q: How many accidents did the driver who had the highest number accidents in the Canadian Grand Prix have?
EVIDENCE: number of accidents refers to the number where statusid = 3; Canadian Grand Prix refers to the race of name

GOLD: SELECT COUNT(T1.driverId) FROM results AS T1 INNER JOIN races AS T2 on T1.raceId = T2.raceId INNER JOIN status AS T3 on T1.statusId = T3.statusId WHERE T3.statusId = 3 AND T2.name = 'Canadian Grand Prix' GROUP BY T1.driverId ORDER BY COUNT(T1.driverId) DESC LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. First, I need to understand what's being asked:
   - Find the number of accidents (where statusid = 3)
   - For the Canadian Grand Prix race
   - Among all drivers who had accidents in this race, find the driver with the highest number of accidents
   - Return how many accidents that driver had

2. Looking at the schema:
   - The `status` table has statusId and status text, where statusid = 3 corresponds to 'Accident'
   - The `races` table has race information including the name 'Canadian Grand Prix'
   - The `results` table connects races, drivers, and status
   - I need to join these tables to find accidents in the Canadian Grand Prix

3. Steps to build the query:
   - Find the raceId for 'Canadian Grand Prix' from the races table
   - Find the statusId for 'Accident' from the status table
   - Join results with races and status to find all accidents in Canadian Grand Prix
   - Group by driverId to count accidents per driver
   - Order by count descending and take the top driver
   - Return just the count of accidents for that driver

Let me write the query:

```sql

FROM results r
JOIN races ra ON r.raceId = ra.raceId
JOIN status s ON r.statusId = s.statusId
WHERE ra.name = 'Canadian Grand Prix' 
  AND s.status = 'Accident'
GROUP BY r.driverId
ORDER BY COUNT(*) DESC
LIMIT 1;
```

--- [259] db=superhero difficulty=challenging ---
Q: What is the percentage of superheroes who act in their own self-interest or make decisions based on their own moral code? Indicate how many of the said superheroes were published by Marvel Comics.
EVIDENCE: published by Marvel Comics refers to publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics'; superheroes who act in their own self-interest or make decisions based on their own moral code refers to alignment = 'Bad'; calculation = MULTIPLY(DIVIDE(SUM(alignment = 'Bad); count(id)), 100)
GOLD: SELECT (CAST(COUNT(*) AS REAL) * 100 / (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM superhero)), CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN T2.publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS REAL) FROM superhero AS T1 INNER JOIN publisher AS T2 ON T1.publisher_id = T2.id INNER JOIN alignment AS T3 ON T3.id = T1.alignment_id WHERE T3.alignment = 'Bad'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Find superheroes with alignment = 'Bad' (self-interest/moral code)
   - Calculate the percentage of all superheroes who are 'Bad'
   - Count how many of these 'Bad' superheroes are published by 'Marvel Comics'

2. **Identifying the tables needed:**
   - `superhero` table - contains superhero info including alignment_id and publisher_id
   - `alignment` table - to filter for alignment = 'Bad'
   - `publisher` table - to filter for publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics'

3. **Steps to build the query:**
   - First, I need to count all superheroes with alignment = 'Bad'
   - Then, I need to count how many of those are published by 'Marvel Comics'
   - Calculate the percentage: (count of 'Bad' superheroes / total superheroes) * 100

4. **Join strategy:**
   - Join superhero with alignment table to filter by alignment = 'Bad'
   - Join superhero with publisher table to filter by publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics'

Let me write the query:

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN p.publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / COUNT(s.id) AS percentage,
    SUM(CASE WHEN p.publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS marvel_count
FROM superhero s
JOIN alignment a ON s.alignment_id = a.id
JOIN publisher p ON s.publisher_id = p.id
WHERE a.alignment = 'Bad';
```

--- [260] db=superhero difficulty=challenging ---
Q: Between DC and Marvel Comics, which publisher has published more superheroes? Find the difference in the number of superheroes they have published.
EVIDENCE: DC refers to publisher_name = 'DC Comics'; Marvel Comics refers to publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics'; calculation = SUBTRACT(SUM(publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics'), SUM(publisher_name = 'DC Comics'))
GOLD: SELECT SUM(CASE WHEN T2.publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) - SUM(CASE WHEN T2.publisher_name = 'DC Comics' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) FROM superhero AS T1 INNER JOIN publisher AS T2 ON T1.publisher_id = T2.id
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find which publisher has published more superheroes and calculate the difference.

Let me think through this step by step:

1. First, I need to count the number of superheroes for each publisher
2. Then I need to find the difference between Marvel Comics and DC Comics counts
3. The question asks for "which publisher has published more" and "the difference"

Looking at the schema:
- The `superhero` table has a `publisher_id` that references the `publisher` table
- The `publisher` table has `publisher_name`

I need to:
1. Join `superhero` with `publisher` to get publisher names
2. Count superheroes for each publisher
3. Calculate the difference between Marvel Comics and DC Comics counts

Since the question asks for "which publisher has published more" and "the difference", I should return the difference, which will be positive if Marvel has more and negative if DC has more.

```sql

    SUM(CASE WHEN p.publisher_name = 'Marvel Comics' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) - 
    SUM(CASE WHEN p.publisher_name = 'DC Comics' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS difference

WHERE p.publisher_name IN ('Marvel Comics', 'DC Comics');
```

--- [271] db=superhero difficulty=moderate ---
Q: What is the hero's full name with the highest attribute in strength?
EVIDENCE: highest attribute in strength refers to MAX(attribute_value) WHERE attribute_name = 'strength';
GOLD: SELECT T1.full_name FROM superhero AS T1 INNER JOIN hero_attribute AS T2 ON T1.id = T2.hero_id INNER JOIN attribute AS T3 ON T2.attribute_id = T3.id WHERE T3.attribute_name = 'Strength' ORDER BY T2.attribute_value DESC LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the hero's full name with the highest attribute value for strength.

Let me think through this step by step:

1. First, I need to identify the tables involved:
   - `superhero` table contains `full_name`
   - `attribute` table contains `attribute_name` 
   - `hero_attribute` table links heroes to their attributes and contains `attribute_value`

2. I need to:
   - Find the attribute_id for 'Strength' from the `attribute` table
   - Join `hero_attribute` with `superhero` to get the full names
   - Filter for only 'Strength' attributes
   - Find the maximum attribute_value
   - Return the full_name of the hero with that maximum value

3. The joins needed:
   - `hero_attribute` joins with `superhero` on hero_id = id
   - `hero_attribute` joins with `attribute` on attribute_id = id

4. The conditions:
   - attribute_name = 'Strength' (case-insensitive comparison might be needed)
   - Need to find the maximum attribute_value

5. Since the question asks for "the hero's full name", I should return only the full_name column.

Let me write the query:

```sql
SELECT s.full_name
FROM superhero s
JOIN hero_attribute ha ON s.id = ha.hero_id
JOIN attribute a ON ha.attribute_id = a.id
WHERE LOWER(a.attribute_name) = 'strength'
ORDER BY ha.attribute_value DESC
LIMIT 1;
```

GOLD: SELECT T1.eye_colour_id, T1.hair_colour_id, T1.skin_colour_id FROM superhero AS T1 INNER JOIN publisher AS T2 ON T2.id = T1.publisher_id INNER JOIN gender AS T3 ON T3.id = T1.gender_id WHERE T2.publisher_name = 'Dark Horse Comics' AND T3.gender = 'Female'
PRED_SQL:

I need to find the eyes, hair, and skin colour of all female superheroes published by Dark Horse Comics.

Let me think through this step by step:

1. I need to join the superhero table with the colour table three times:
   - Once for eye colour (eye_colour_id)
   - Once for hair colour (hair_colour_id) 
   - Once for skin colour (skin_colour_id)

2. I need to filter for:
   - Gender = 'Female' (need to join with gender table)
   - Publisher = 'Dark Horse Comics' (need to join with publisher table)

3. The question asks for:
   - Eyes (eye colour)
   - Hair (hair colour)
   - Skin colour (skin colour)

- superhero table has gender_id that references gender table
- superhero table has publisher_id that references publisher table

```sql
    c2.colour AS hair,
    c3.colour AS skin

  AND p.publisher_name = 'Dark Horse Comics';
```

Q: What is the percentage of blue female superheroes among all female superheroes?
EVIDENCE: percentage = MULTIPLY(DIVIDE(SUM(colour = 'Blue' WHERE gender = 'Female'), COUNT(gender = 'Female')), 100); blue refers to the color = 'Blue' WHERE skin_colour_id = colour.id; female refers to gender = 'Female';
GOLD: SELECT CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN T3.colour = 'Blue' THEN T1.id ELSE NULL END) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T1.id) FROM superhero AS T1 INNER JOIN gender AS T2 ON T1.gender_id = T2.id INNER JOIN colour AS T3 ON T1.skin_colour_id = T3.id WHERE T2.gender = 'Female'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the question**: I need to find the percentage of female superheroes who have blue skin among all female superheroes.

2. **Key information from the question**:
   - "blue" refers to skin_colour_id = colour.id where colour = 'Blue'
   - "female" refers to gender = 'Female'
   - I need to calculate: (count of female superheroes with blue skin / total count of female superheroes) * 100

3. **Tables I need**:
   - `superhero` table: contains gender_id and skin_colour_id
   - `gender` table: to identify 'Female' gender
   - `colour` table: to identify 'Blue' colour

4. **Steps to build the query**:
   - Join superhero with gender table to filter for females
   - Join superhero with colour table to identify blue skin
   - Count total female superheroes
   - Count female superheroes with blue skin
   - Calculate the percentage

5. **Approach**:
   - Use conditional aggregation or subqueries
   - The numerator should count females with blue skin
   - The denominator should count all females
   - Multiply by 100 for percentage

Let me write the query:

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN c.colour = 'Blue' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / COUNT(*) AS percentage
FROM superhero s
JOIN gender g ON s.gender_id = g.id
LEFT JOIN colour c ON s.skin_colour_id = c.id
WHERE g.gender = 'Female'
```

- `hero_attribute` → `attribute` on `hero_attribute.attribute_id = attribute.id`

```sql
SELECT a.attribute_name, ha.attribute_value
FROM superhero s
JOIN hero_attribute ha ON s.id = ha.hero_id
JOIN attribute a ON ha.attribute_id = a.id
WHERE s.superhero_name = '3-D Man';
```

Q: Which superheroes have blue eyes with brown hair?
EVIDENCE: which superheroes refers to superhero_name; blue eyes refers to color = 'Blue' and color.id = eye_colour_id; brown hair refers to color = 'Brown' and color.id = hair_colour_id;
GOLD: SELECT T1.superhero_name FROM superhero AS T1 INNER JOIN colour AS T2 ON T1.eye_colour_id = T2.id INNER JOIN colour AS T3 ON T1.hair_colour_id = T3.id WHERE T2.colour = 'Blue' AND T3.colour = 'Brown'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find superheroes who have blue eyes and brown hair. Let me break this down step by step:

1. I need to find superheroes with blue eyes:
   - Blue eyes means `eye_colour_id` in the `superhero` table matches the `id` in the `colour` table where `colour = 'Blue'`

2. I need to find superheroes with brown hair:
   - Brown hair means `hair_colour_id` in the `superhero` table matches the `id` in the `colour` table where `colour = 'Brown'`

3. I need to join the `superhero` table with the `colour` table twice:
   - Once to match eye color
   - Once to match hair color

4. The question asks for "which superheroes", which refers to `superhero_name`

Let me construct the query:

- Start with the `superhero` table
- Join with `colour` table twice (once for eye colour, once for hair colour)
- Filter for eye colour = 'Blue' and hair colour = 'Brown'
- Select only the `superhero_name` as requested

```sql
SELECT s.superhero_name
FROM superhero s
JOIN colour eye_colour ON s.eye_colour_id = eye_colour.id
JOIN colour hair_colour ON s.hair_colour_id = hair_colour.id
WHERE eye_colour.colour = 'Blue' 
  AND hair_colour.colour = 'Brown';
```

EVIDENCE: missing weight data refers to weight_kg = 0 OR T1.weight_kg = NULL; difference = SUBTRACT(SUM(colour.id = 7), SUM(colour.id = 1)); blue eyes refers to eye_colour_id WHERE colour.id = 7; no eye color refers to eye_colour_id WHERE colour.id = 1;
GOLD: SELECT SUM(CASE WHEN T2.id = 7 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) - SUM(CASE WHEN T2.id = 1 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) FROM superhero AS T1 INNER JOIN colour AS T2 ON T1.eye_colour_id = T2.id WHERE T1.weight_kg = 0 OR T1.weight_kg is NULL
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Find superheroes with missing weight data (weight_kg = 0 OR weight_kg IS NULL)
   - Among these superheroes, count how many have blue eyes (eye_colour_id = 7)
   - Among these superheroes, count how many have no eye color (eye_colour_id = 1)
   - Calculate the difference: (count of blue eyes) - (count of no eye color)

2. **Key points from the schema:**
   - The `superhero` table has `weight_kg` and `eye_colour_id` columns
   - `eye_colour_id` references the `colour` table's `id` column
   - Blue eyes corresponds to `colour.id = 7`
   - No eye color corresponds to `colour.id = 1`

3. **Query approach:**
   - Filter superheroes with missing weight data
   - Count those with blue eyes (eye_colour_id = 7)
   - Count those with no eye color (eye_colour_id = 1)
   - Calculate the difference

4. **Implementation:**
   - Use conditional aggregation with CASE statements to count each category
   - Apply the WHERE clause for missing weight data
   - Calculate the difference in the SELECT clause

```sql
SELECT 
    SUM(CASE WHEN s.eye_colour_id = 7 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) - 
    SUM(CASE WHEN s.eye_colour_id = 1 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS difference
FROM superhero s
WHERE s.weight_kg = 0 OR s.weight_kg IS NULL
```

Q: Among the posts with a score of over 5, what is the percentage of them being owned by an elder user?

GOLD: SELECT CAST(SUM(IIF(T2.Age > 65, 1, 0)) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T1.Id) FROM posts AS T1 INNER JOIN users AS T2 ON T1.OwnerUserId = T2.Id WHERE T1.Score > 5
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the percentage of posts with a score over 5 that are owned by users older than 65.

Let me break this down step by step:

1. First, I need to identify posts with a score over 5
2. Among those posts, I need to find how many are owned by users older than 65
3. Calculate the percentage: (count of posts owned by users > 65 / total count of posts with score > 5) * 100

Looking at the schema:
- The `posts` table has `Score` and `OwnerUserId` columns
- The `users` table has `Id` and `Age` columns
- I need to join these tables to connect posts to user ages

Steps:
1. Join `posts` with `users` on `OwnerUserId` = `Id`
2. Filter for posts where `Score` > 5
3. Count total posts with score > 5
4. Count posts with score > 5 AND OwnerUserId's user age > 65
5. Calculate the percentage

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN u.Age > 65 THEN 1 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / COUNT(*) AS percentage
FROM posts p
JOIN users u ON p.OwnerUserId = u.Id
WHERE p.Score > 5
```

   - Find a comment made by user 23853 at exactly 9:08:18 on 2013/7/12
   - Check if the post that this comment was made on was "well-finished"
   - "Well-finished" means the post has a ClosedDate (not NULL)
   - "Not well-finished" means the post has no ClosedDate (ClosedDate IS NULL)

2. Looking at the schema:
   - Comments table has: Id, PostId, Score, Text, CreationDate, UserId
   - Posts table has: Id, ClosedDate (among other columns)
   - I need to join these tables to get the post information for the comment

3. Steps to build the query:
   - Find the comment where UserId = 23853 and CreationDate = '2013-07-12 09:08:18.0'

   - Return whether the post was well-finished (ClosedDate IS NOT NULL)

```sql

    WHEN p.ClosedDate IS NOT NULL THEN 'well-finished' 
    ELSE 'not well-finished' 
END AS result
FROM comments c
JOIN posts p ON c.PostId = p.Id
WHERE c.UserId = 23853 
AND c.CreationDate = '2013-07-12 09:08:18.0'
```

```sql
    p.Title,
    c.Text AS Comment,
    AVG(p.ViewCount) OVER() AS AverageViewCount
FROM posts p
JOIN comments c ON p.Id = c.PostId
WHERE p.Tags = '<humor>'
```

2. "having at least 1000 views" - The posts should have ViewCount >= 1000
3. "user refers to UserId" - We need to return the UserId

1. First, I need to identify posts that have exactly one post history entry (using GROUP BY and HAVING COUNT(*) = 1)

3. Finally, I need to get the UserId (OwnerUserId) of those posts

- Use HAVING COUNT(*) = 1

PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:

1. I need to find badges where Name = 'Student'
2. I need to count how many 'Student' badges were given in 2010
3. I need to count how many 'Student' badges were given in 2011
4. I need to calculate the percentage difference using the formula provided

Let me analyze the formula:
- percentage difference = Subtract (Divide(Count(Name where Year(Date) = 2010), Count (Name)) *100, Divide(Count(Name where Year(Date) = 2011), Count(Name)) * 100)

This seems to be calculating: (percentage in 2010 - percentage in 2011)

Actually, looking more carefully at the formula, it's:
(Count(2010) / Count(total)) * 100 - (Count(2011) / Count(total)) * 100

Let me re-read... the formula is: Subtract (Divide(Count(Name where Year(Date) = 2010), Count (Name)) *100, Divide(Count(Name where Year(Date) = 2011), Count(Name)) * 100)

This means: (Count_2010 / Total_Count) * 100 - (Count_2011 / Total_Count) * 100

4. Calculate percentage for 2010: (count_2010 / total) * 100
5. Calculate percentage for 2011: (count_2011 / total) * 100
6. Calculate difference: percentage_2010 - percentage_2011

```sql

    CAST((COUNT(CASE WHEN strftime('%Y', Date) = '2010' THEN 1 END) * 100.0 / COUNT(*)) - 
         (COUNT(CASE WHEN strftime('%Y', Date) = '2011' THEN 1 END) * 100.0 / COUNT(*)) AS REAL) AS percentage_difference
```

GOLD: SELECT AVG(T1.UpVotes), AVG(T1.Age) FROM users AS T1 INNER JOIN ( SELECT OwnerUserId, COUNT(*) AS post_count FROM posts GROUP BY OwnerUserId HAVING post_count > 10) AS T2 ON T1.Id = T2.OwnerUserId
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the question**: I need to find:
   - Average up votes for users who created more than 10 posts
   - Average age for users who created more than 10 posts

2. **Key information from the question**:
   - "creating more than 10 post refers to Count(UserId) > 10" - This means I need to count posts per user and filter users with more than 10 posts
   - "average of the up votes = Divide (Sum(UpVotes), Count (UserId))" - Average up votes = Total up votes / Number of users
   - "average age = Divide (Sum(Age), Count(UserId))" - Average age = Total age / Number of users

   - `posts` table: to count posts per user (OwnerUserId)
   - `users` table: to get UpVotes and Age information

   - Then, I need to get the up votes and age for these users (from users table)

   - Group by UserId to count posts per user

```sql
    AVG(u.Age) AS average_age
FROM users u
```

PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:

   - `Id` (the post ID I need to return)
   - `FavoriteCount` (what makes a post "valuable")
   - `CreaionDate` (to filter for 2010)
   - `OwnerUserId` (to link to users table)

2. I need to:
   - Filter posts where the year of `CreaionDate` is 2010
   - Find the post with the maximum `FavoriteCount` among those
   - Join with the `users` table to get the owner's display name

4. To get the year from a datetime in SQLite, I can use `strftime('%Y', CreationDate)`.

5. I need to return only the Id and OwnerDisplayName as requested.

Here's my approach:
- Filter posts from 2010
- Order by FavoriteCount descending
- Take the first result (LIMIT 1)
- Join with users table to get the display name

```sql
SELECT p.Id, u.DisplayName
FROM posts p
JOIN users u ON p.OwnerUserId = u.Id
WHERE strftime('%Y', p.CreationDate) = '2010'
ORDER BY p.FavoriteCount DESC
LIMIT 1;
```

GOLD: SELECT T1.name, T1.artist, T1.isPromo FROM cards AS T1 INNER JOIN rulings AS T2 ON T1.uuid = T2.uuid WHERE T1.isPromo = 1 AND T1.artist = (SELECT artist FROM cards WHERE isPromo = 1 GROUP BY artist HAVING COUNT(DISTINCT uuid) = (SELECT MAX(count_uuid) FROM ( SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT uuid) AS count_uuid FROM cards WHERE isPromo = 1 GROUP BY artist ))) LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the card with the most ruling information and check if it's a promotional printing.

Let me think through this step by step:

1. First, I need to understand the relationship between cards and rulings:
   - The `rulings` table has a `uuid` column that references `cards.uuid`
   - Each ruling is associated with a card through this UUID

2. To find the card with the most ruling information:
   - I need to count the number of rulings for each card
   - Group by card UUID and count the rulings
   - Order by count descending and take the top result

3. From the question, I need to return:
   - The card name
   - The artist
   - Whether it's a promotional printing (isPromo = 1)

4. I need to join the cards table with rulings table to count rulings per card

Let me construct the query:

```sql
SELECT 
    c.name,
    c.artist,
    c.isPromo
FROM cards c
JOIN rulings r ON c.uuid = r.uuid
GROUP BY c.uuid, c.name, c.artist, c.isPromo
ORDER BY COUNT(r.id) DESC
LIMIT 1;
```

Q: Calculate the percentage of the cards availabe in Chinese Simplified.
EVIDENCE: Chinese Simplified' is the language; percentage = Divide(Sum(id where language = 'Chinese Simplified'), Count(id)) *100
GOLD: SELECT CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN T2.language = 'Chinese Simplified' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T1.id) FROM cards AS T1 INNER JOIN foreign_data AS T2 ON T1.uuid = T2.uuid
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to calculate the percentage of cards available in Chinese Simplified language.

   - The `foreign_data` table contains translations with a `language` column
   - The `foreign_data` table has a `uuid` column that links to the `cards` table
   - I need to count how many cards have Chinese Simplified translations

2. To calculate the percentage:
   - Numerator: Count of cards that have at least one Chinese Simplified translation
   - Denominator: Total count of all cards
   - Formula: (Numerator / Denominator) * 100

3. Looking at the schema:
   - `foreign_data` table has `language` column with example values including 'Chinese Simplified'
   - `foreign_data` table has `uuid` that links to `cards` table
   - I need to count distinct cards (using uuid) that have Chinese Simplified translations

- The `foreign_data` table contains translations for cards
- Each row in `foreign_data` represents a translation for a specific card (via uuid)

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN fd.language = 'Chinese Simplified' THEN c.id END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / 
    COUNT(DISTINCT c.id) AS percentage
FROM cards c

```

```sql
JOIN legalities l ON c.id = l.uuid
JOIN rulings r ON c.id = r.uuid
WHERE l.format = 'premodern'
  AND r.text = 'This is a triggered mana ability.'
  AND c.side IS NULL
```

--- [371] db=card_games difficulty=challenging ---
Q: What percentage of cards with format commander and legal status do not have a content warning?
EVIDENCE: do not have a content warning refers to hasContentWarning = 0; percentage refers to DIVIDE(COUNT(hasContentWarning = 0),COUNT(ID))*100 where format = 'commander' AND Status = 'legal';
GOLD: SELECT CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN T1.hasContentWarning = 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T1.id) FROM cards AS T1 INNER JOIN legalities AS T2 ON T1.uuid = T2.uuid WHERE T2.format = 'commander' AND T2.status = 'Legal'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the percentage of cards with format 'commander' and legal status that do not have a content warning.

Let me break down the requirements:
1. I need to look at cards that have format 'commander' and status 'legal'
2. Among those cards, I need to calculate what percentage have hasContentWarning = 0
3. The percentage formula is: (COUNT of cards with hasContentWarning = 0) / (COUNT of all cards) * 100

Looking at the schema:
- The `legalities` table contains format and status information
- The `cards` table contains hasContentWarning information
- These tables are connected via uuid

Steps to write the query:
1. Join cards and legalities tables on uuid
2. Filter for format = 'commander' and status = 'legal'
3. Calculate the percentage of cards where hasContentWarning = 0

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN c.hasContentWarning = 0 THEN 1 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / COUNT(*) AS percentage
FROM cards c
JOIN legalities l ON c.uuid = l.uuid
WHERE l.format = 'commander' 
  AND l.status = 'legal';
```

--- [372] db=card_games difficulty=challenging ---
Q: What percentage of cards without power are in French?
EVIDENCE: in French refers to language = 'French'; cards without power refers to power IS NULL OR power = '*'; percentage = DIVIDE(COUNT(language = 'French' and power is NULL or power = '*'), COUNT( power is NULL or power = '*'))*100
GOLD: SELECT CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN T2.language = 'French' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T1.id) FROM cards AS T1 INNER JOIN foreign_data AS T2 ON T1.uuid = T2.uuid WHERE T1.power IS NULL OR T1.power = '*'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the percentage of cards without power that are in French.

Let me break down the requirements:
1. "cards without power" means power IS NULL OR power = '*'
2. "in French" means language = 'French' in the foreign_data table
3. I need to calculate: (COUNT of French cards without power / COUNT of all cards without power) * 100

Let me think through the steps:
1. First, I need to identify cards without power from the cards table
2. Then, I need to join with foreign_data table to check which ones are in French
3. Count the total cards without power
4. Count the French cards without power
5. Calculate the percentage

Looking at the schema:
- The `cards` table has a `power` column
- The `foreign_data` table has `language` and `uuid` columns
- The `uuid` column links cards to their foreign data

Here's my approach:
1. Join cards with foreign_data on uuid
2. Filter for cards where power IS NULL OR power = '*'
3. Count total cards without power
4. Count French cards without power
5. Calculate percentage

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN fd.language = 'French' THEN 1 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / COUNT(*) AS percentage
FROM cards c
LEFT JOIN foreign_data fd ON c.uuid = fd.uuid
WHERE c.power IS NULL OR c.power = '*'
```

   - The `cards` table has a `setCode` column that links to `sets.code`

   - Total number of cards in Coldsnap set
   - Number of cards with convertedManaCost = 7 in Coldsnap set

- `cards` table has `setCode` that references `sets.code`

--- [393] db=card_games difficulty=moderate ---
Q: Which of the play format has the highest number of banned status? Indicate the play format and the names of all the card meet the condition.
EVIDENCE: play format refers to format; banned status refers to status = 'Banned'; the highest number of banned status refers to MAX(COUNT(status = 'Banned'))
GOLD: WITH MaxBanned AS (SELECT format, COUNT(*) AS count_banned FROM legalities WHERE status = 'Banned' GROUP BY format ORDER BY COUNT(*) DESC LIMIT 1) SELECT T2.format, T1.name FROM cards AS T1 INNER JOIN legalities AS T2 ON T2.uuid = T1.uuid INNER JOIN MaxBanned MB ON MB.format = T2.format WHERE T2.status = 'Banned'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find which play format (format) has the highest number of cards with banned status, and also list the names of all cards that meet this condition.

Let me break down the steps:

1. First, I need to understand the relationships:
   - The `legalities` table contains format and status information for cards
   - The `cards` table contains card names
   - Both tables are connected via uuid

2. I need to:
   - Count how many cards are banned in each format
   - Find the format with the maximum count
   - Get all card names that have banned status in that format

3. Looking at the schema:
   - `legalities` table has: id, format, status, uuid
   - `cards` table has: uuid, name
   - I need to join these tables on uuid

4. Approach:
   - First, count banned cards per format
   - Find the format with maximum count
   - Then get all cards with banned status in that format

Let me write the query:

```sql
WITH banned_counts AS (
    SELECT 
        format,
        COUNT(*) as banned_count
    FROM legalities
    WHERE status = 'Banned'
    GROUP BY format
),
max_format AS (
    SELECT format
    FROM banned_counts
    WHERE banned_count = (SELECT MAX(banned_count) FROM banned_counts)
)
SELECT 
    l.format,
    c.name
FROM legalities l
JOIN cards c ON l.uuid = c.uuid
WHERE l.status = 'Banned' 
AND l.format = (SELECT format FROM max_format)
ORDER BY c.name;
```

EVIDENCE: single-bonded molecules refers to bond_type = '-' ; average number of oxygen atom = AVG(element = 'o')
GOLD: SELECT AVG(oxygen_count) FROM (SELECT T1.molecule_id, COUNT(T1.element) AS oxygen_count FROM atom AS T1 INNER JOIN bond AS T2 ON T1.molecule_id = T2.molecule_id  WHERE T2.bond_type = '-' AND T1.element = 'o'  GROUP BY T1.molecule_id) AS oxygen_counts

   - Calculate the average of these counts

   - Join with atom to count oxygen atoms per molecule
   - Group by molecule_id to count atoms per molecule
   - Calculate average of the counts

- Get molecules that have at least one single bond
- For each such molecule, count its oxygen atoms
- Average those counts

```sql

FROM (
    SELECT m.molecule_id, COUNT(a.atom_id) as oxygen_count
    FROM molecule m
    JOIN bond b ON m.molecule_id = b.molecule_id
    JOIN atom a ON m.molecule_id = a.molecule_id
    WHERE b.bond_type = '-' AND a.element = 'o'
    GROUP BY m.molecule_id
) subquery
```

Q: What percentage of carcinogenic-type molecules does not contain fluorine?
EVIDENCE: label = '+' mean molecules are carcinogenic; contain fluorine refers to element = 'f'; percentage = DIVIDE(SUM(element = 'f') * 100, COUNT(molecule_id)) where label = '+'; Should consider the distinct atoms when counting;
GOLD: SELECT CAST(COUNT(DISTINCT CASE WHEN T1.element <> 'f' THEN T2.molecule_id ELSE NULL END) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(DISTINCT T2.molecule_id) FROM atom AS T1 INNER JOIN molecule AS T2 ON T1.molecule_id = T2.molecule_id WHERE T2.label = '+'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the question**: 
   - We need to find the percentage of carcinogenic molecules (label = '+') that do NOT contain fluorine (element = 'f')
   - "Carcinogenic" means label = '+'
   - "Contain fluorine" means having at least one atom with element = 'f'
   - We want the percentage of carcinogenic molecules that do NOT contain fluorine

2. **Key points**:
   - Only consider molecules with label = '+'
   - Count distinct molecules (not atoms) 
   - A molecule contains fluorine if it has at least one atom with element = 'f'
   - We want molecules that are carcinogenic AND do NOT contain fluorine
   - Percentage = (count of carcinogenic molecules without fluorine * 100) / (total count of carcinogenic molecules)

3. **Approach**:
   - First, identify all carcinogenic molecules (label = '+')
   - Then, identify which of these contain fluorine (have atoms with element = 'f')
   - Count those that DON'T contain fluorine
   - Calculate the percentage

   - Find molecules that DO contain fluorine
   - Subtract to get molecules that DON'T contain fluorine
   - Calculate percentage

Let me think about this more carefully:

- Total carcinogenic molecules = COUNT(DISTINCT molecule_id) WHERE label = '+'
- Carcinogenic molecules WITH fluorine = COUNT(DISTINCT molecule_id) WHERE molecule_id IN (SELECT DISTINCT molecule_id FROM atom WHERE element = 'f') AND label = '+'
- Carcinogenic molecules WITHOUT fluorine = Total carcinogenic - Carcinogenic with fluorine
- Percentage = (molecules without fluorine * 100) / total carcinogenic molecules

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN a.molecule_id IS NULL THEN 1 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / COUNT(m.molecule_id) AS percentage
FROM molecule m
LEFT JOIN (
    SELECT DISTINCT molecule_id
    FROM atom
    WHERE element = 'f'
) a ON m.molecule_id = a.molecule_id
WHERE m.label = '+'
```

EVIDENCE: hydrogen refers to element = 'h'; TR206 is the molecule id; percentage = DIVIDE(SUM(element = 'h'), COUNT(atom_id)) as percent where molecule_id = 'TR206'

PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:

1. I need to find the percentage of hydrogen atoms (element = 'h') in molecule TR206
2. The formula given is: percentage = DIVIDE(SUM(element = 'h'), COUNT(atom_id)) as percent
3. This means I need to:

   - Count the total number of atoms in molecule TR206
   - Calculate the percentage

   - The `atom` table has `atom_id`, `molecule_id`, and `element`
   - I need to filter by `molecule_id = 'TR206'`
   - I need to count atoms where `element = 'h'` and total atoms

5. In SQLite, I can use:
   - SUM(CASE WHEN element = 'h' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) to count hydrogen atoms
   - COUNT(atom_id) to count total atoms
   - Cast to REAL to ensure decimal division
   - Round to 4 decimal places

Let me write the query:


PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:

1. I need to find the bond type that accounts for the majority of bonds in molecule TR010
2. I need to count how many bonds of each type exist for molecule TR010
3. I need to identify which bond type has the maximum count
4. I also need to determine if the molecule is carcinogenic (this information is in the `label` column of the `molecule` table)

Let me break down the approach:
- First, I'll join the `bond` table with the `molecule` table to filter for molecule_id = 'TR010'
- Then I'll group by bond_type and count them
- Find the bond_type with the maximum count

Here's my approach:
1. Filter bonds for molecule TR010
2. Group by bond_type and count occurrences
3. Order by count descending and take the first one
4. Join with molecule table to get the label

```sql
SELECT 
    b.bond_type,
    m.label
FROM bond b
JOIN molecule m ON b.molecule_id = m.molecule_id
WHERE b.molecule_id = 'TR010'

```

   - I need to count all iodine atoms

   - `atom` table has `atom_id` and `element`
   - `connected` table links atoms through bonds
   - Each row in `connected` represents a bond between two atoms

     - Get the elements of these atoms from the `atom` table

3. **Query approach**:
   - Start with the `bond` table to filter for `bond_type = '#'`
   - Join with `connected` table on `bond_id` to get the atom pairs
   - Join with `atom` table twice - once for `atom_id` and once for `atom_id2` to get both elements
   - Since the question asks for "the elements", I should return both elements involved in each triple bond

4. **What to return**: The question asks for "the elements", so I need to return the elements of both atoms in each triple bond.

Let me construct the query:

```sql
SELECT DISTINCT a1.element, a2.element
FROM bond b
JOIN connected c ON b.bond_id = c.bond_id
JOIN atom a1 ON c.atom_id = a1.atom_id
JOIN atom a2 ON c.atom_id2 = a2.atom_id
WHERE b.bond_type = '#'
```

Q: What proportion of single bonds are carcinogenic? Please provide your answer as a percentage with five decimal places.
EVIDENCE: single bond refers to bond_type = '-'; label = '+' mean molecules are carcinogenic; proportion = DIVIDE(SUM(label = '+') * 100, COUNT(bond_id)) where bond_type = '-'
GOLD: SELECT ROUND(CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN T2.label = '+' THEN T1.bond_id ELSE NULL END) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T1.bond_id),5) FROM bond AS T1 INNER JOIN molecule AS T2 ON T1.molecule_id = T2.molecule_id WHERE T1.bond_type = '-'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Single bonds are defined as `bond_type = '-'`
   - Carcinogenic molecules are those with `label = '+'`
   - I need to find the proportion of single bonds that are in carcinogenic molecules
   - The proportion formula is: (COUNT of single bonds in carcinogenic molecules * 100) / (COUNT of all single bonds)

2. **Understanding the relationships:**
   - The `bond` table has `bond_type` and `molecule_id`
   - The `molecule` table has `molecule_id` and `label`
   - I need to join these tables to connect bonds to molecule labels

3. **Steps to build the query:**
   - First, I need to identify all single bonds (`bond_type = '-'`)
   - Then, I need to count how many of these single bonds are in carcinogenic molecules (`label = '+'`)
   - Finally, calculate the percentage

4. **Query construction:**
   - Join `bond` and `molecule` tables on `molecule_id`
   - Filter for single bonds (`bond_type = '-'`)
   - Count total single bonds
   - Count single bonds in carcinogenic molecules
   - Calculate the percentage

Let me write the query:

```sql

    CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN m.label = '+' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) * 100.0 AS REAL) / COUNT(b.bond_id) AS proportion

JOIN molecule m ON b.molecule_id = m.molecule_id
WHERE b.bond_type = '-';
```

GOLD: SELECT COUNT(T1.atom_id) FROM atom AS T1 INNER JOIN molecule AS T2 ON T1.molecule_id = T2.molecule_id INNER JOIN bond AS T3 ON T2.molecule_id = T3.molecule_id WHERE T3.bond_type = '#' AND T1.element IN ('p', 'br')

   - These molecules must contain either phosphorus (element = 'p') or bromine (element = 'br')
   - Count the total number of atoms in these molecules

2. **Understanding the schema relationships:**
   - `molecule` table has molecule_id and label
   - `bond` table has bond_id, molecule_id, and bond_type
   - `atom` table has atom_id, molecule_id, and element
   - `connected` table links atoms through bonds

GOLD: SELECT CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN T.element = 'cl' THEN T.atom_id ELSE NULL END) AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T.atom_id) FROM ( SELECT T1.atom_id, T1.element FROM atom AS T1 INNER JOIN molecule AS T2 ON T1.molecule_id = T2.molecule_id INNER JOIN bond AS T3 ON T2.molecule_id = T3.molecule_id WHERE T3.bond_type = '-' ) AS T
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:

2. **Key relationships**:
   - Atoms are in the `atom` table with their elements
   - Bonds are in the `bond` table with bond types
   - Atoms are connected by bonds through the `connected` table

3. **Steps to solve**:
   - First, I need to identify all atoms that are part of single bonds (bond_type = '-')
   - Then, among those atoms, calculate what percentage have element = 'cl'
   - The percentage formula is: (count of chlorine atoms in single bonds / total count of atoms in single bonds) * 100

4. **Join strategy**:

   - Join with `bond` to filter for single bonds (bond_type = '-')

   - Count chlorine atoms in single bonds


2. **Key points**:

Q: What is the ratio of Hydrogen elements in molecule ID TR006? List the ratio with its label.
EVIDENCE: hydrogen refers to element = 'h'; ratio = DIVIDE(SUM(element = 'h'), count(element)) where molecule_id = 'TR006' ; label = '+' mean molecules are carcinogenic; label = '-' means molecules are non-carcinogenic
GOLD: WITH SubQuery AS (SELECT DISTINCT T1.atom_id, T1.element, T1.molecule_id, T2.label FROM atom AS T1 INNER JOIN molecule AS T2 ON T1.molecule_id = T2.molecule_id WHERE T2.molecule_id = 'TR006') SELECT CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN element = 'h' THEN atom_id ELSE NULL END) AS REAL) / (CASE WHEN COUNT(atom_id) = 0 THEN NULL ELSE COUNT(atom_id) END) AS ratio, label FROM SubQuery GROUP BY label
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me think through this step by step.

1. I need to find the ratio of Hydrogen elements (element = 'h') in molecule ID 'TR006'
2. The ratio is defined as: SUM(element = 'h') / COUNT(element)
3. I also need to include the label of this molecule
4. The molecule table has molecule_id and label
5. The atom table has molecule_id and element

Steps to write the query:
1. Join molecule and atom tables on molecule_id
2. Filter for molecule_id = 'TR006'
3. Calculate the ratio of hydrogen elements
4. Get the label for this molecule

Let me break down the ratio calculation:
- COUNT(element) will give total number of atoms in the molecule
- SUM(CASE WHEN element = 'h' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) will count hydrogen atoms
- The ratio is hydrogen_count / total_count

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST(SUM(CASE WHEN a.element = 'h' THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS FLOAT) / COUNT(a.element) AS ratio,

WHERE m.molecule_id = 'TR006'
GROUP BY m.label;
```

GOLD: SELECT T1.sname, T2.`Charter Funding Type` FROM satscores AS T1 INNER JOIN frpm AS T2 ON T1.cds = T2.CDSCode WHERE T2.`District Name` LIKE 'Riverside%' GROUP BY T1.sname, T2.`Charter Funding Type` HAVING CAST(SUM(T1.AvgScrMath) AS REAL) / COUNT(T1.cds) > 400
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:

   - Find schools in Riverside county
   - These schools must have an average math SAT score > 400
   - Return the funding type of these schools

2. **Key information needed**:
   - Schools in Riverside county (from schools table)
   - Average math SAT scores (from satscores table)
   - Funding type (from schools table)

   - Filter for Riverside county
   - Filter for average math scores > 400

   - Looking at the schema, funding type is in the schools table as "FundingType"

- schools table has: County, FundingType, CDSCode
- satscores table has: AvgScrMath, cds (which references CDSCode)

The question mentions "Average of average math = sum(average math scores) / count(schools)" but looking at the context, it seems to be asking for schools where the average math score is > 400, not the overall average of averages.

```sql
SELECT DISTINCT s.FundingType
FROM schools s
JOIN satscores ss ON s.CDSCode = ss.cds
WHERE s.County = 'Riverside' 
  AND ss.AvgScrMath > 400
```

Q: What is the average score in writing for the schools that were opened after 1991 or closed before 2000? List the school names along with the score. Also, list the communication number of the schools if there is any.
EVIDENCE: Communication number refers to phone number.

PRED_SQL:

   - Average score in writing (from satscores table)
   - School names (from satscores table)
   - Communication number (phone number) from schools table
   - For schools that were opened after 1991 OR closed before 2000

   - `satscores` - for writing scores and school names
   - `schools` - for phone numbers, open dates, and close dates

--- [447] db=california_schools difficulty=challenging ---
Q: Consider the average difference between K-12 enrollment and 15-17 enrollment of schools that are locally funded, list the names and DOC type of schools which has a difference above this average.
EVIDENCE: Difference between K-12 enrollment and 15-17 enrollment can be computed by `Enrollment (K-12)` - `Enrollment (Ages 5-17)`
GOLD: SELECT T2.School, T2.DOC FROM frpm AS T1 INNER JOIN schools AS T2 ON T1.CDSCode = T2.CDSCode WHERE T2.FundingType = 'Locally funded' AND (T1.`Enrollment (K-12)` - T1.`Enrollment (Ages 5-17)`) > (SELECT AVG(T3.`Enrollment (K-12)` - T3.`Enrollment (Ages 5-17)`) FROM frpm AS T3 INNER JOIN schools AS T4 ON T3.CDSCode = T4.CDSCode WHERE T4.FundingType = 'Locally funded')
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. First, I need to understand what's being asked:
   - Calculate the difference between K-12 enrollment and 5-17 enrollment for each school
   - Find the average of these differences across all schools
   - Find schools where this difference is above the average
   - Return the school names and DOC types for these schools

2. Looking at the schema:
   - The `frpm` table has `Enrollment (K-12)` and `Enrollment (Ages 5-17)` columns
   - The `schools` table has `DOCType` column and `School` column
   - These tables can be joined on `CDSCode`

3. Key considerations:
   - Need to filter for locally funded schools (from `frpm` table, but I need to check which column contains funding info)
   - Looking at the schema, `frpm` table has `Charter Funding Type` column
   - The question mentions "locally funded" schools, so I need to filter where `Charter Funding Type` = 'Locally funded'
   - Actually, looking more carefully, the `schools` table has `FundingType` column, which might be more appropriate
   - But the question specifically mentions "locally funded" schools, and in `frpm` table there's `Charter Funding Type` column

4. Let me re-read the question more carefully:
   - "Consider the average difference between K-12 enrollment and 15-17 enrollment of schools that are locally funded"
   - So I need to:
     - Filter schools that are locally funded
     - Calculate the difference for each school
     - Find the average of these differences
     - Find schools with difference above this average
     - Return school names and DOC types

5. Looking at the tables:
   - `frpm` table has `Charter Funding Type` column
   - `schools` table has `FundingType` column
   - Both tables have `CDSCode` for joining
   - The question asks for "names" which would be `School Name` in `frpm` or `School` in `schools`
   - The question asks for "DOC type" which would be `DOCType` in `schools`

6. I need to join `frpm` and `schools` tables on `CDSCode` to get both the enrollment data and the DOCType.

7. The difference is: `Enrollment (K-12)` - `Enrollment (Ages 5-17)`

Let me write the query:

```sql
WITH differences AS (
    SELECT 
        f.CDSCode,
        f.`School Name`,
        s.DOCType,
        f.`Enrollment (K-12)` - f.`Enrollment (Ages 5-17)` AS diff
    FROM frpm f
    JOIN schools s ON f.CDSCode = s.CDSCode
    WHERE f.`Charter Funding Type` = 'Locally funded'
),
avg_diff AS (
    SELECT AVG(diff) AS average_diff
    FROM differences
)
SELECT 
    d.`School Name`,
    d.DOCType
FROM differences d
CROSS JOIN avg_diff a
WHERE d.diff > a.average_diff;
```

   - The `frpm` table has `FRPM Count (K-12)` and `Enrollment (K-12)` columns

--- [454] db=california_schools difficulty=simple ---
Q: List the names of virtual schools that are among the top 5 in their respective counties based on average reading scores.
EVIDENCE: Exclusively virtual refers to Virtual = 'F'; respective counties means PARTITION BY County
GOLD: SELECT School FROM (SELECT T2.School,T1.AvgScrRead, RANK() OVER (PARTITION BY T2.County ORDER BY T1.AvgScrRead DESC) AS rnk FROM satscores AS T1 INNER JOIN schools AS T2 ON T1.cds = T2.CDSCode WHERE T2.Virtual = 'F' ) ranked_schools WHERE rnk <= 5
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Find virtual schools (Virtual = 'F')
   - Among these, find the top 5 in each county based on average reading scores
   - Return the names of these schools

2. **Identifying the relevant tables:**
   - `schools` table: Contains school names and Virtual status
   - `satscores` table: Contains average reading scores and county information
   - These tables can be joined on CDSCode

3. **Key conditions:**
   - Virtual = 'F' (exclusive virtual schools)
   - Need to partition by County
   - Rank by AvgScrRead (average reading scores) within each county
   - Top 5 in each county

4. **Approach:**
   - Join schools and satscores tables
   - Filter for virtual schools (Virtual = 'F')
   - Use window functions to rank schools by average reading scores within each county
   - Select only the top 5 from each county
   - Return only the school names as requested

Let me construct the query:

```sql
WITH ranked_schools AS (
    SELECT 
        s.School,
        s.County,
        ss.AvgScrRead,
        ROW_NUMBER() OVER (PARTITION BY s.County ORDER BY ss.AvgScrRead DESC) as rank
    FROM schools s
    JOIN satscores ss ON s.CDSCode = ss.cds
    WHERE s.Virtual = 'F'
)
SELECT School
FROM ranked_schools
WHERE rank <= 5
ORDER BY County, rank;
```

   - From `schools` table: `OpenDate`, `County`, `DOC`
   - We need to filter by:
     - `OpenDate` year = 1980
     - `County` = 'Alameda'
     - `DOC` = '52' (note: DOC is text type based on schema)

3. **Steps to write the query:**
   - Count schools that opened in 1980 in Alameda County with DOC = '52'
   - Divide that count by 12 to get the monthly average

4. **Important considerations:**
   - The OpenDate is stored as a date type, so I need to extract the year
   - DOC is stored as text, so I need to compare with '52'
   - County is stored as text, so I need to compare with 'Alameda'

```sql
SELECT COUNT(*) / 12.0 AS monthly_average
FROM schools
WHERE strftime('%Y', OpenDate) = '1980'
  AND County = 'Alameda'
  AND DOC = '52';
```

GOLD: SELECT COUNT(T2.School) FROM frpm AS T1 INNER JOIN schools AS T2 ON T1.CDSCode = T2.CDSCode WHERE T2.County = 'Los Angeles' AND T2.Charter = 0 AND CAST(T1.`Free Meal Count (K-12)` AS REAL) * 100 / T1.`Enrollment (K-12)` < 0.18
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Find non-chartered schools (Charter = 0)
   - In the county of Los Angeles
   - With percent of eligible free meals for K-12 less than 0.18%
   - Return the total number of such schools

2. **Key information from schema:**
   - The `frpm` table contains the FRPM data including `Charter School (Y/N)` and `County Name`
   - The `schools` table contains the `Charter` field and `County` field
   - The percent calculation is: `Free Meal Count (K-12)` * 100 / `Enrollment (K-12)`
   - We need to join these tables using CDSCode

3. **Join strategy:**
   - Join `frpm` and `schools` tables on CDSCode
   - Filter for County Name = 'Los Angeles' (from frpm table)
   - Filter for Charter = 0 (from schools table)
   - Filter for percent < 0.18

2. I need to find the school with the highest longitude value. Since the question mentions "highest longitude" and "maximum absolute longitude value", I should consider the absolute value of longitude to find the school that is farthest east or west.

- Return only the `GSoffered` column for that school

GOLD: SELECT T2.account_id FROM loan AS T1 INNER JOIN account AS T2 ON T1.account_id = T2.account_id WHERE STRFTIME('%Y', T1.date) = '1997' AND T2.frequency = 'POPLATEK TYDNE' ORDER BY T1.amount LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Find accounts with approved loans in 1997
   - Among those accounts, find the ones with the lowest approved amount
   - These accounts must have 'POPLATEK TYDNE' (weekly issuance) frequency
   - The question asks to "list out the accounts" - so we need to return account_id

2. **Key information from schema:**
   - Loan table has: loan_id, account_id, date, amount, duration, payments, status
   - Account table has: account_id, district_id, frequency, date
   - 'POPLATEK TYDNE' is a value in the frequency column of account table
   - Loan status is mentioned as 'approved' (though not explicitly defined, it's implied by the context)

   - Filter for loans with date in 1997
   - Filter for accounts with frequency = 'POPLATEK TYDNE'

   - Return all accounts that have this minimum amount

   - First, I need to identify accounts with loans in 1997 and weekly issuance
   - Then find the minimum amount among these
   - Finally, return all accounts with that minimum amount

Let me write the query:

```sql
SELECT DISTINCT a.account_id
FROM account a
JOIN loan l ON a.account_id = l.account_id
WHERE strftime('%Y', l.date) = '1997'
  AND a.frequency = 'POPLATEK TYDNE'
  AND l.amount = (
    SELECT MIN(l2.amount)
    FROM account a2
    JOIN loan l2 ON a2.account_id = l2.account_id
    WHERE strftime('%Y', l2.date) = '1997'
      AND a2.frequency = 'POPLATEK TYDNE'
  )
```

Q: For the branch which located in the south Bohemia with biggest number of inhabitants, what is the percentage of the male clients?

GOLD: SELECT CAST(SUM(T1.gender = 'M') AS REAL) * 100 / COUNT(T1.client_id) FROM client AS T1 INNER JOIN district AS T2 ON T1.district_id = T2.district_id WHERE T2.A3 = 'south Bohemia' GROUP BY T2.A4 ORDER BY T2.A4 DESC LIMIT 1
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the percentage of male clients for the branch located in "south Bohemia" with the biggest number of inhabitants.

Let me break this down step by step:

1. First, I need to identify the district in "south Bohemia" with the biggest number of inhabitants (A4)
2. Then, I need to find all clients in that district
3. Calculate the percentage of male clients (gender = 'M') among all clients in that district

- The `district` table has A3 (region) and A4 (number of inhabitants)
- The `client` table has `district_id` which links to `district`
- The `client` table has `gender` column

2. Count all clients in that district
3. Count male clients (gender = 'M') in that district
4. Calculate percentage

Let me write the query:

```sql

    CAST(COUNT(CASE WHEN c.gender = 'M' THEN 1 END) AS FLOAT) * 100 / COUNT(*) AS percentage
FROM client c
WHERE c.district_id = (

    FROM district 
    WHERE A3 = 'south Bohemia' 
    ORDER BY CAST(A4 AS INTEGER) DESC 
    LIMIT 1
)
```

--- [478] db=financial difficulty=challenging ---
Q: For the client whose loan was approved first in 1993/7/5, what is the increase rate of his/her account balance from 1993/3/22 to 1998/12/27?
EVIDENCE: Increase rate of his/her account balance = [(balance of date A - balance of date B) / balance of Date B] * 100%
GOLD: SELECT CAST((SUM(IIF(T3.date = '1998-12-27', T3.balance, 0)) - SUM(IIF(T3.date = '1993-03-22', T3.balance, 0))) AS REAL) * 100 / SUM(IIF(T3.date = '1993-03-22', T3.balance, 0)) FROM loan AS T1 INNER JOIN account AS T2 ON T1.account_id = T2.account_id INNER JOIN trans AS T3 ON T3.account_id = T2.account_id WHERE T1.date = '1993-07-05'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the increase rate of account balance for the client whose loan was approved first on 1993/7/5, from 1993/3/22 to 1998/12/27.

Let me break this down step by step:

1. First, I need to find the client whose loan was approved first on 1993/7/5
2. Then, I need to find the account associated with this client
3. Get the balance from 1993/3/22 and 1998/12/27 for that account
4. Calculate the increase rate using the formula: [(balance_A - balance_B) / balance_B] * 100%

Let me trace through the relationships:
- Loans are in the `loan` table with `date` column
- Loans are linked to accounts via `account_id`
- Accounts are linked to clients via the `disp` table (disposition)
- Transactions contain balance information via the `trans` table

Steps:
1. Find the loan with date = '1993-07-05' (first loan approved on that date)
2. Get the account_id from that loan
3. Find the client_id through the disposition table
4. Get balances from trans table for the specified dates

Let me write the query:

```sql
WITH first_loan_client AS (
    SELECT l.account_id
    FROM loan l
    WHERE l.date = '1993-07-05'
    LIMIT 1
),
client_account AS (
    SELECT d.client_id, d.account_id
    FROM disp d
    JOIN first_loan_client flc ON d.account_id = flc.account_id
    LIMIT 1
),
balances AS (
    SELECT 
        (SELECT balance FROM trans t1 WHERE t1.account_id = (SELECT account_id FROM client_account) AND t1.date = '1993-03-22') AS balance_start,
        (SELECT balance FROM trans t2 WHERE t2.account_id = (SELECT account_id FROM client_account) AND t2.date = '1998-12-27') AS balance_end
)
SELECT 
    CASE 
        WHEN balance_start IS NOT NULL AND balance_end IS NOT NULL AND balance_start != 0 
        THEN ((balance_end - balance_start) * 100.0 / balance_start)
        ELSE NULL 
    END AS increase_rate
FROM balances;
```

4. **Status**: Approved loans (need to determine what status means "approved")
5. **What to count**: Number of loans

- The `account` table has `frequency` column
- The `loan` table has `date`, `amount`, and `status` columns
- The `loan` table is connected to `account` via `account_id`

GOLD: SELECT DISTINCT T1.A2 FROM district AS T1 INNER JOIN account AS T2 ON T1.district_id = T2.district_id INNER JOIN trans AS T3 ON T2.account_id = T3.account_id WHERE T3.type = 'VYDAJ' AND T3.date LIKE '1996-01%' ORDER BY A2 ASC LIMIT 10
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me think through this step by step.

   - Find non-credit card withdrawals (type = 'VYDAJ')
   - For January 1996 (date LIKE '1996-01%')
   - Group by district names (A2)
   - Get the top 10 withdrawals
   - Need to sum up the withdrawal amounts by district

2. **Identifying the tables needed:**
   - `trans` table: contains transaction data with type, date, and amount
   - `account` table: links transactions to accounts
   - `district` table: contains district names (A2)

3. **Understanding the relationships:**
   - `trans.account_id` → `account.account_id`
   - `account.district_id` → `district.district_id`

4. **Query construction:**
   - Join trans → account → district
   - Filter for type = 'VYDAJ' (withdrawals)
   - Filter for date LIKE '1996-01%'
   - Group by district name (A2)
   - Sum the amounts
   - Order by sum descending

```sql

LIMIT 10;
```

   - `amount` column has the transaction amount
   - `date` column has the transaction date
   - `account_id` links to the account
   - To get account holders, I need to connect through the `disp` table (disposition table)

```sql
    WHERE operation = 'VYBER KARTOU'
```

--- [492] db=financial difficulty=challenging ---
Q: What was the growth rate of the total amount of loans across all accounts for a male client between 1996 and 1997?
EVIDENCE: Growth rate = (sum of amount_1997 - sum of amount_1996) / (sum of amount_1996) * 100%; Male refers to gender = 'M'
GOLD: SELECT CAST((SUM(CASE WHEN STRFTIME('%Y', T1.date) = '1997' THEN T1.amount ELSE 0 END) - SUM(CASE WHEN STRFTIME('%Y', T1.date) = '1996' THEN T1.amount ELSE 0 END)) AS REAL) * 100 / SUM(CASE WHEN STRFTIME('%Y', T1.date) = '1996' THEN T1.amount ELSE 0 END) FROM loan AS T1 INNER JOIN account AS T2 ON T1.account_id = T2.account_id INNER JOIN disp AS T3 ON T3.account_id = T2.account_id INNER JOIN client AS T4 ON T4.client_id = T3.client_id WHERE T4.gender = 'M' AND T3.type = 'OWNER'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
I need to find the growth rate of total loan amounts for male clients between 1996 and 1997.

Let me break down the steps:

1. First, I need to identify male clients (gender = 'M') from the client table
2. Find all accounts associated with these male clients through the disp table
3. Get all loans for these accounts from the loan table
4. Calculate the sum of loan amounts for 1996 and 1997 separately
5. Apply the growth rate formula: ((sum_1997 - sum_1996) / sum_1996) * 100

Let me trace through the relationships:
- client (client_id) → disp (client_id) 
- disp (account_id) → loan (account_id)
- loan has a date field and amount field

Looking at the schema more carefully, I notice that the loan table has a 'date' field and an 'amount' field. I need to filter loans by year and sum the amounts.

The growth rate formula is: ((sum of amount_1997 - sum of amount_1996) / sum of amount_1996) * 100

Let me write the query:

```sql
SELECT 
    CAST((SUM(CASE WHEN strftime('%Y', l.date) = '1997' THEN l.amount ELSE 0 END) - 
          SUM(CASE WHEN strftime('%Y', l.date) = '1996' THEN l.amount ELSE 0 END)) AS REAL) * 100.0 / 
    SUM(CASE WHEN strftime('%Y', l.date) = '1996' THEN l.amount ELSE 0 END) AS growth_rate
FROM client c
JOIN disp d ON c.client_id = d.client_id
JOIN loan l ON d.account_id = l.account_id
WHERE c.gender = 'M'
```

RESPONSE:
Let me break down this question step by step:

1. **Female clients**: I need to find clients where gender = 'F'
2. **Oldest clients**: I need to find the client with the earliest birth_date (minimum birth_date)
3. **Lowest average salary**: I need to find the district with the lowest A11 value (average salary)
4. **Account numbers**: I need to return the account_id of these clients

Let me trace through the relationships:
- Client table has gender and birth_date, and links to district via district_id
- District table has A11 (average salary)
- Client connects to accounts through the disp table
- Account table has account_id

Steps to solve:
1. Find the minimum birth_date among female clients
2. Find the minimum A11 value (lowest average salary) among districts
3. Find female clients who are oldest (have minimum birth_date)
4. Among those oldest female clients, find the ones who live in districts with lowest average salary
5. Get the account numbers for these clients

Let me think about this more carefully:
- The question asks for "account numbers of female clients who are oldest and have lowest average salary"
- This means I need to find female clients who are oldest AND live in districts with lowest average salary
- The oldest female client would be the one with the earliest birth_date among all female clients
- The lowest average salary would be the minimum A11 value in the district table

Actually, re-reading the question: "Female clients who are oldest and have lowest average salary" - this seems to be asking for:
1. Female clients who are oldest (earliest birth_date)
2. AND who live in districts with the lowest average salary

So I need to:
1. Find the oldest female client(s) (minimum birth_date among females)
2. Find the district(s) with the lowest average salary (minimum A11)
3. Find female clients who are oldest AND live in districts with lowest average salary
4. Return their account numbers

```sql
SELECT DISTINCT a.account_id
FROM client c
JOIN district d ON c.district_id = d.district_id
JOIN disp di ON c.client_id = di.client_id
JOIN account a ON di.account_id = a.account_id
WHERE c.gender = 'F'
  AND c.birth_date = (
    SELECT MIN(birth_date)
    FROM client
    WHERE gender = 'F'
  )
  AND d.A11 = (
    SELECT MIN(A11)
    FROM district
  )
```

Q: What is the average amount of loan which are still on running contract with statement issuance after each transaction?
EVIDENCE: status = 'C' stands for running contract, OK so far; status = 'D' stands for running contract, client in debt. 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU' stands for issuance after transaction
GOLD: SELECT AVG(T2.amount) FROM account AS T1 INNER JOIN loan AS T2 ON T1.account_id = T2.account_id WHERE T2.status IN ('C', 'D') AND T1.frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this question step by step:
