   - Find loans that are "still on running contract" 
   - These loans should have "issuance after each transaction" (which corresponds to frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU')
   - Calculate the average amount of these loans

2. **Key information from the question:**
   - Status = 'C' means running contract (as stated in the question)
   - Status = 'D' means running contract with client in debt (as stated in the question)
   - Frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU' means issuance after transaction
   - We need average amount of loans

3. **Looking at the schema:**
   - The `loan` table has: loan_id, account_id, date, amount, duration, payments, status
   - The `account` table has: account_id, district_id, frequency, date
   - The `loan` table is connected to `account` via account_id

4. **Query construction:**
   - Join loan and account tables on account_id
   - Filter for status = 'C' (running contract)
   - Filter for frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU' (issuance after transaction)
   - Calculate average amount

Wait, let me re-read the question more carefully. It says "status = 'C' stands for running contract, OK so far; status = 'D' stands for running contract, client in debt." This seems contradictory, but I'll follow the question's logic that both C and D represent running contracts, and we want the average amount of loans that are running contracts with issuance after transaction.

Actually, re-reading: "status = 'C' stands for running contract, OK so far; status = 'D' stands for running contract, client in debt." This seems to be saying that both C and D represent running contracts, but D means running contract with client in debt. The question asks for "running contract" which would include both C and D.

But then it says "What is the average amount of loan which are still on running contract with statement issuance after each transaction?"

Let me interpret this as:
- Loans that are still running (status = 'C' or 'D')
- With frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU' (issuance after transaction)
- Calculate average amount

However, looking at the schema more carefully, the `loan` table doesn't have a frequency column. The frequency is in the `account` table. So I need to join loan with account to get the frequency.

Let me re-read the question once more:
"status = 'C' stands for running contract, OK so far; status = 'D' stands for running contract, client in debt. 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU' stands for issuance after transaction"

The question is asking for loans that are:
1. Still on running contract (so status = 'C' or 'D')
2. With issuance after transaction (frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU')

```sql
SELECT AVG(l.amount)
FROM loan l
JOIN account a ON l.account_id = a.account_id
WHERE l.status IN ('C', 'D') 
AND a.frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU'
```

--- [497] db=financial difficulty=moderate ---
Q: Provide the IDs and age of the client with high level credit card, which is eligible for loans.
EVIDENCE: the credit card is high-level refers to card.type = 'gold'; eligible for loans refers to disp.type = 'OWNER'
GOLD: SELECT T1.client_id, STRFTIME('%Y', CURRENT_TIMESTAMP) - STRFTIME('%Y', T3.birth_date) FROM disp AS T1 INNER JOIN card AS T2 ON T2.disp_id = T1.disp_id INNER JOIN client AS T3 ON T1.client_id = T3.client_id WHERE T2.type = 'gold' AND T1.type = 'OWNER'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me think through this step by step.

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Find clients with high-level credit cards (card.type = 'gold')
   - These clients must be eligible for loans (disp.type = 'OWNER')
   - Return: client IDs and ages

2. **Understanding the relationships:**
   - Client table has client_id and birth_date
   - Card table has card_id, disp_id, and type
   - Disp table has disp_id, client_id, and type
   - To connect these: client → disp → card

3. **Steps to build the query:**
   - Start with the client table to get client_id and calculate age
   - Join with disp table on client_id to find ownership relationships
   - Join with card table on disp_id to find card information
   - Filter for card.type = 'gold' and disp.type = 'OWNER'
   - Calculate age from birth_date

4. **Age calculation:**
   - In SQLite, we can calculate age using: (strftime('%Y', 'now') - strftime('%Y', birth_date)) 
   - But we need to be more precise to handle the exact date

5. **Building the query:**
   - SELECT client_id and age
   - JOIN client → disp → card
   - WHERE conditions for card.type = 'gold' AND disp.type = 'OWNER'

```sql
SELECT 
    c.client_id,
    (strftime('%Y', 'now') - strftime('%Y', c.birth_date)) AS age
FROM client c
JOIN disp d ON c.client_id = d.client_id
JOIN card cd ON d.disp_id = cd.disp_id
WHERE cd.type = 'gold' 
    AND d.type = 'OWNER'
```

Q: For accounts in 1993 with statement issued after transaction, list the account ID, district name and district region.
EVIDENCE: Records about district names could be found in A2; A3 contains the information about regions. 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU' stands for issuance after transaction
GOLD: SELECT T1.account_id, T2.A2, T2.A3 FROM account AS T1 INNER JOIN district AS T2 ON T1.district_id = T2.district_id WHERE T1.frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU' AND STRFTIME('%Y', T1.date)= '1993'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me break down this problem step by step:

1. **Understanding the requirements:**
   - Find accounts from 1993
   - These accounts must have "POPLATEK PO OBRATU" as frequency (which means issuance after transaction)
   - Need to return: account ID, district name (A2), and district region (A3)

2. **Identifying the tables needed:**
   - `account` table: contains account_id, district_id, and frequency
   - `district` table: contains district_id, A2 (district name), and A3 (region)

3. **Understanding the conditions:**
   - `account.date` should be in 1993
   - `account.frequency` should be 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU'

4. **Join strategy:**
   - Join `account` and `district` tables on district_id

5. **Building the query:**
   - SELECT: account_id, A2 (district name), A3 (district region)
   - FROM: account joined with district
   - WHERE: account.date LIKE '1993%' and account.frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU'

```sql
SELECT 
    a.account_id,
    d.A2 AS district_name,
    d.A3 AS district_region
FROM account a
JOIN district d ON a.district_id = d.district_id
WHERE a.date LIKE '1993%' 
    AND a.frequency = 'POPLATEK PO OBRATU';
```

--- [499] db=financial difficulty=moderate ---
Q: From Year 1995 to 2000, who are the accounts holders from 'east Bohemia'. State the account ID the frequency of statement issuance.
EVIDENCE: Accounts holder refers to the person who own this account.
GOLD: SELECT T1.account_id, T1.frequency FROM account AS T1 INNER JOIN district AS T2 ON T1.district_id = T2.district_id WHERE T2.A3 = 'east Bohemia' AND STRFTIME('%Y', T1.date) BETWEEN '1995' AND '2000'
PRED_SQL: 
RESPONSE:
Let me think through this step by step.

1. **Understanding the question:**
   - Find account holders (owners) from 'east Bohemia' region
   - Time period: Year 1995 to 2000
   - Need to return: account ID, frequency of statement issuance

2. **Identifying the tables needed:**
   - `account` table: contains account_id and frequency
   - `district` table: contains region information (A3 column)
   - Need to join these tables through district_id

3. **Key relationships:**
   - `account.district_id` → `district.district_id`
   - `account.date` needs to be between 1995 and 2000

4. **Filtering conditions:**
   - Region = 'east Bohemia' (from district.A3)
   - Account date between 1995 and 2000

5. **What to return:**
   - account_id
   - frequency

Let me construct the query:

```sql
SELECT a.account_id, a.frequency
FROM account a
JOIN district d ON a.district_id = d.district_id
WHERE d.A3 = 'east Bohemia'
  AND a.date >= '1995-01-01'
  AND a.date <= '2000-12-31'
```
